    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15774306864643084357">Hilarious, shocking and hugely entertaining, Reheated Cabbage has all the classic Irvine Welsh ingredients.<br/><br/>In these pages you can enjoy Christmas dinner with Begbie, and see how warmly Franco greets his sister's boyfriend and the news of their engagement. You will discover, in 'The Rosewell Incident', how aliens addicted to Embassy Regal have Midlothian under surveillance,</span>
  <span id="freeText15774306864643084357" style="display:none">Hilarious, shocking and hugely entertaining, Reheated Cabbage has all the classic Irvine Welsh ingredients.<br /><br />In these pages you can enjoy Christmas dinner with Begbie, and see how warmly Franco greets his sister's boyfriend and the news of their engagement. You will discover, in 'The Rosewell Incident', how aliens addicted to Embassy Regal have Midlothian under surveillance, and plan to install the local casuals as the new governors of Planet Earth. You will not be surprised to read that a televised Hibs vs. Hearts game might matter more to one character than the life of his wife, or that two guys fighting over a beautiful girl might agree -- on reflection, and after a few pills and many pints of lager -- that their friendship is actually more important. And you will be delighted to welcome back 'Juice' Terry Lawson, and to watch what happens when he meets his old nemesis, retired schoolmaster Albert Black, under the strobe-lights of a Miami Beach nightclub.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15774306864643084357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1948849606?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Vaughn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Vaughn" href="/user/show/4025601-matthew-vaughn">Matthew Vaughn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4025601-matthew-vaughn?shelf=general-fiiction">general-fiiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4025601-matthew-vaughn?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1948849606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17969778240138136029">This book was great! I've become a huge fan of Welsh and I really enjoyed these new/old stories involving various characters in his universe. The novella at the end, I am Miami, is like a sequel to both Porno and Glue. Juice Terry is one of Welsh's best characters and I found this new adventure of his to be very entertaining!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_596242289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/596242289" />
    <a title="Dane Cobain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19638210-dane-cobain"><img alt="Dane Cobain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571333550p2/19638210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/596242289?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dane Cobain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dane Cobain" href="/user/show/19638210-dane-cobain">Dane Cobain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer596242289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9290179299898139328">Welsh is back. It's time for me to blather aboot this eminently readable collection of Welsh's short stories, spanning from 1994-2000. And what a cracker it is, too.<br/><br/>Written in Welsh's typical vernacular, complete with his idiosyncratic sense of spelling and grammar, Reheated Cabbage captures the essence of Welsh's early writing in a fantastic collection of short stories which cover everything from pills and pals to aliens addicted to Embassy cigarettes who've learned the niceties of human cultur</span>
  <span id="freeText9290179299898139328" style="display:none">Welsh is back. It's time for me to blather aboot this eminently readable collection of Welsh's short stories, spanning from 1994-2000. And what a cracker it is, too.<br /><br />Written in Welsh's typical vernacular, complete with his idiosyncratic sense of spelling and grammar, Reheated Cabbage captures the essence of Welsh's early writing in a fantastic collection of short stories which cover everything from pills and pals to aliens addicted to Embassy cigarettes who've learned the niceties of human culture from a Scottish geezer who's hiding out from the police on-board their ship.<br /><br />There's death too, of course - the collection starts with the story of a man who's so keen to catch the Hibs v.s. Hearts game that he leads his wife into the path of an oncoming train, and you can expect to witness the death of a junkie in the sad surroundings of a Scottish house party.<br /><br />But above all else, Reheated Cabbage offers you a chance to catch up with old friends, whether you're eating Christmas dinner with Begbie or you're catching up with Juice Terry and Carl 'N-Sign' Ewart in Miami.<br /><br />Meeting up with a middle-aged Carl and Terry is made all the more sweet by the reappearance of their former nemesis - Mr. Black from their schooldays. He's not quite the imposing figure that he used to be - in fact, by the end of his story, you'll just want to give him a hug.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9290179299898139328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1275713453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15506803314913435248">I am a committed Irvine Welsh fan. I think what he does with the Scottish dialect is incredibly creative. I have never read another author who I could so clearly hear while I am reading. It is a pretty fun experience. Plus, he is very funny, in an incredibly dark way. The other thing he does which I really like is he uses the same characters in a lot of his stories. They are all set in the same place, among the same group of friends. So the stories in this collection have some of the guys from "</span>
  <span id="freeText15506803314913435248" style="display:none">I am a committed Irvine Welsh fan. I think what he does with the Scottish dialect is incredibly creative. I have never read another author who I could so clearly hear while I am reading. It is a pretty fun experience. Plus, he is very funny, in an incredibly dark way. The other thing he does which I really like is he uses the same characters in a lot of his stories. They are all set in the same place, among the same group of friends. So the stories in this collection have some of the guys from "Trainspotting," including a great story about Begbie coming to his mother's for Christmas dinner. Terry Lawson is also in it, and he was also tangentially in "Trainspotting" and much more significantly in "Glue." It's a complete world, and a pretty fascinating, if horrifying one. The stories here are kind of hit-and-miss, some are much better than others, but it's always worth the trip.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15506803314913435248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17495756275999335422">Extremely entertaining collection. Like many others, I was a Welsh obsessive as a mid-90s teenager: many of the pieces collected here are welcome reminders of the thrill I experienced first reading him. Only one, 'The Rosewell Incident,' is a misstep: hated it back in '96ish, when I first read it, and it hasn't improved with age. But the rest were gross, vulgar, energetic. A delight.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10536946187822154095">It sometimes happens that story collections turn out to be a bit lumpy in the sense that the pieces not always complement each other smoothly. This is one of those. However, each story on its own is great, especially the first – what a masterpiece! I have never laughed so much about such a tragic event. It’s all in how you tell it…<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_220922121" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/220922121" />
    <a title="Jeff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5046987-jeff"><img alt="Jeff" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220922121?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff" href="/user/show/5046987-jeff">Jeff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338027" href="/book/show/6570524-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220922121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9315930590193792580">I didn't like Trainspotting. It was ok, I just didn't get into it. At the time, not knowing that it was based on a book, I thought it would have been better as a book, that prose would have been a better medium in which to really flesh out the characters and capture all the nuances of the situations. <br/><br/>Well this book, Reheated Cabbage, is exactly what I thought Trainspotting had the potential to be. It is witty, tragic, nuanced, depraved, depressing, insightful, and brilliant. The characters, thro</span>
  <span id="freeText9315930590193792580" style="display:none">I didn't like Trainspotting. It was ok, I just didn't get into it. At the time, not knowing that it was based on a book, I thought it would have been better as a book, that prose would have been a better medium in which to really flesh out the characters and capture all the nuances of the situations. <br /><br />Well this book, Reheated Cabbage, is exactly what I thought Trainspotting had the potential to be. It is witty, tragic, nuanced, depraved, depressing, insightful, and brilliant. The characters, thrown into mostly unexceptional circumstances, are so well drawn out that the reader feels he knows each one personally, knows each character's entire life story before even picking up the book. And to say the stories' circumstances are unexceptional, is not to say they are boring or uninteresting. In fact it's the exact opposite. The stories are mostly based around fairly ordinary situations with just enough of wist to make them different from the everyday. And Welsh writes them in such a way as to make them extraordinary.<br /><br />Irvine Welsh is a true master of his craft and RC is a perfect example of his brilliance. The stories in RC are, in many ways, reminiscent of those of Raymond Carver and Ernest Hemingway. Indeed, one can almost envision Welsh as Carver or Hemingway reincarnated as a modern day, working class Scotsman. <br /><br />The only reason it rates 4.5 out of 5 stars is that the final story, the novella I Am Miami, is something of a let down. It is brilliant in its own right and quite probably worthy of 5 stars alone, but having already torn through the previous shorter, more rapidly-paced stories, stories thick with Scottish brogue and filthy with the stench of realism, I Am Miami is slow and more detached, more proper in a way. It's a departure that's unexpected and can make the gears grind to a halt. Had the stories been rearranged, with I Am Miami among the first few, and perhaps with the stories with the heaviest brogue toward the end, it would almost certainly rate the full 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9315930590193792580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_189342304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189342304" />
    <a title="Colin N." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5876178-colin-n"><img alt="Colin N." src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/189342304?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colin N." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colin N." href="/user/show/5876178-colin-n">Colin N.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338027" href="/book/show/6570524-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189342304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4624095890849028737">"Reheated Cabbage" collects a handful of short stories that Welsh has published elsewhere over the past few years, and like any such anthology there is variation in the quality and cohesion of the book as a whole. There are a couple of throwaway stories and a really silly (yet still kind of amusing) story involving aliens. But overall this is definitely a collection to read because the last three stories are really quite excellent. Especially the final story, "I am Miami," which might be one of </span>
  <span id="freeText4624095890849028737" style="display:none">"Reheated Cabbage" collects a handful of short stories that Welsh has published elsewhere over the past few years, and like any such anthology there is variation in the quality and cohesion of the book as a whole. There are a couple of throwaway stories and a really silly (yet still kind of amusing) story involving aliens. But overall this is definitely a collection to read because the last three stories are really quite excellent. Especially the final story, "I am Miami," which might be one of the best things Welsh has ever written. <br /><br /><br /><br />Welsh returns to some of his characters from his previous novels, which is always welcome. So we get a brief return to the twisted mind of Begbie in one story. And a return of Ewart and Juice Terry in another. The final 3 stories really are wonderful and perfectly Welshian. The first involves a disaster that occurs at a party that is very reminiscent of the stories in "Trainspotting." The tale is disturbing, morbidly humorous, and a typical Welsh story of drugs and violence. Another is a very funny comic battle between two rivals for the attentions of a woman. <br /><br /><br /><br />And finally the last story, which takes the point of view of Black, a minor character from "Glue," and fleshes him out in a heartbreaking, comical, touching, and twisted tale of an encounter with his former students. Ewart and Terry are such vivid characters it is also nice to revisit them. This really is a superb story and one of the most human and genuine tales (but still with the drugs, sex, and silliness one expects from Welsh) that he has ever written. The book is worth it for this story alone.<br /><br /><br /><br />A good read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4624095890849028737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4110535589724113297" style="display:none"><br />Almost everything in here has been published before in places like “Children of Albion Rovers” and various magazines, extinct or otherwise. This isn’t his strongest collection of stories, I personally think it contains one of his weakest ones in “The Rosewell Incident”, which felt overdone to me. <div id="review_3544689930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3544689930" />
    <a title="Aaron Nash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45707654-aaron-nash"><img alt="Aaron Nash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511167493p2/45707654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3544689930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12701384445135550153">I love Welsh and his short stories are no exception. His characters really make me laugh out loud. There isn't many authors who can amuse me like that. None of the stories here are boring, the return of Begbie and Christmas Dinner around his mother's place was a particular highlight. Crude, rude, smutty and loathsome. All of Welsh's traits are here and it's always good to spend time with his foul creations.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3442912775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3442912775" />
    <a title="JK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2058014-jk"><img alt="JK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604495956p2/2058014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3442912775?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JK" href="/user/show/2058014-jk">JK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099506997" href="/book/show/8861534-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3442912775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11439538366018012344">Here I am again, emerging from the dark pit of human iniquity and psychological torment which I willingly lower myself into when reading a Welsh novel. I’ve just read of the most insane, immoral, and mind-bending situations, I’ve come away muddled and mishandled, and yet I always fucking love it.<br/><br/>We have a collection of some of Welsh’s earlier short stories, each of them differing in tone, setting, and message, but all seeming somehow to be coated in the grime of the human condition. We see some </span>
  <span id="freeText11439538366018012344" style="display:none">Here I am again, emerging from the dark pit of human iniquity and psychological torment which I willingly lower myself into when reading a Welsh novel. I’ve just read of the most insane, immoral, and mind-bending situations, I’ve come away muddled and mishandled, and yet I always fucking love it.<br /><br />We have a collection of some of Welsh’s earlier short stories, each of them differing in tone, setting, and message, but all seeming somehow to be coated in the grime of the human condition. We see some old pals, including Begbie and Juice Terry, and meet some new absolutely mad folk who I’d love to see again.<br /><br />Welsh always seems an expert in digging into the alpha-male psyche and showing us how his scoundrel’s brains work, whilst ripping the pish out them at the same time. Talking your wrecked wife into taking a shortcut over the train tracks so you won’t miss the Hibs game. Starting a scrap in the dentist’s office because you can’t believe this other guy shagged your ex last night. Cracking your sister’s new boyfriend on Christmas day because he hit you on the back to stop you from choking. It’s all fucking hilarious, but there’s some deep-rooted commentary there on male pride, which is worthwhile.<br /><br />This had a similar feel to <i>
  <a href="http://www.book-odyssey.com/2018/09/book-68.html" rel="nofollow noopener">If You Liked School, You’ll Love Work</a>
</i>, where some stories are hits and some are misses, but there’s a pervading sense of Welsh being experimental, and seeing where it gets him. This does involve smacking us with aliens who love a snout, and a dentist getting a hard on when he sees the inside of a woman’s mouth, <i>but</i> in the name of experimentation, it’s a great laugh.<br /><br />A perfect wee injection of darkness and morbidity until we can read more Welsh. Mon then.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11439538366018012344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_489391691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489391691" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2147949-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364148056p2/2147949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489391691?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/2147949-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2147949-victoria?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2147949-victoria?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489391691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer192174538666395016">I’ve read quite a few of Irvine Welsh’s novels: <i>Trainspotting</i>, <i>Porno</i>, <i>Filth</i>, <i>Ecstasy</i> and I can’t help but think that once you’ve read one (or possibly two), you’ve pretty much read them all. Drugs, sex, violence, sexism, homophobia – that kind of car-crash literature that you don’t want to like but somehow can’t help it and of course, is shocking for the sake of being shocking. <br/><br/>	I was hardly surprised, then, when <i>Reheated Cabbage</i>, for the most part, provides much of the same – and not necessaril</span>
  <span id="freeText192174538666395016" style="display:none">I’ve read quite a few of Irvine Welsh’s novels: <i>Trainspotting</i>, <i>Porno</i>, <i>Filth</i>, <i>Ecstasy</i> and I can’t help but think that once you’ve read one (or possibly two), you’ve pretty much read them all. Drugs, sex, violence, sexism, homophobia – that kind of car-crash literature that you don’t want to like but somehow can’t help it and of course, is shocking for the sake of being shocking. <br /><br />	I was hardly surprised, then, when <i>Reheated Cabbage</i>, for the most part, provides much of the same – and not necessarily for a positive result. Even the title is reminiscent of an over-done, soggy and slightly distasteful experience and this proves pretty much the rule for Welsh, as yet again the characters, themes and supposed-shocks are re-hashed, re-visited and once more rammed down your throat. A shame because Welsh, like a good cabbage, has the potential to be crisp and delicious. Don’t get me wrong – I loved Welsh when I first read his work, as his repeated feature upon my book shelf testifies but enough is enough – I’m bored already. Okay, after reading <i>Trainspotting</i>, I leapt into <i>Porno</i> to discover where the characters went but now, after all this time, I don’t care for Begbie and Juice and the admittedly more background crowd being dredged up. <br /><br />	Generally, I dislike collections of short-stories. It feels like the reader has to work a lot harder than with a novel. That bit at the beginning of the novel, when you acquaint yourself with the characters and setting, those moments before you are fully taken in the stream of the word-river, when you are still painfully aware that you are reading – they seem to happen over and over again with short story collections, making you feel like you are putting a heck of a lot more in than you are getting out. So generally, I avoid them. But actually, the end of one story in <i>Reheated Cabbage</i> and the beginning of another was a blessing and a relief – maybe, just maybe, he’ll try something different this time – a new idea? A new character? A new structure? Please, Mr Welsh! Give me something! <br /><br />	And that he did. At least partly. <i>The Roswell Incident</i> and the short novella <i>I Am Miami</i> save this book from a possible 1-star death, for they do indeed offer something different. Of course, Welsh still doesn’t sway completely away from drugs and violence – both featuring heavily in the former and slightly less but still omnipresent in the latter, but the introduction of aliens, familial relationships and even, to a degree, happy endings is a pleasant surprise that induces forgiving feelings and re-ignites a little of the fire for Welsh that the other stories put out. <br /><br />	I do, of course, accept that these are, for the most part, previously published stories that have been brought together for the purpose of this book. In fact, <i>I Am Miami</i>, one of the two that I liked, is the only new story to be published here. However, the bringing them together at all still elicits the above criticisms, whether they are old-hat or not. Besides, the first published story in the book <i>Kissing and Making Up</i> was published after his highly acclaimed <i>Trainspotting</i>. <br /><br />	So, if you’ve read a lot of Irvine Welsh’s work, skip to the two tales mentioned above – they are worth a read, in their own small way. If you are new to Welsh, read them all – you may discover a new love (that given half the chance and a few more novels, will batter you to death with repetitiveness).</span>
  <a data-text-id="192174538666395016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_911548639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/911548639" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8783950-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359487931p2/8783950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/911548639?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/8783950-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099506997" href="/book/show/8861534-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer911548639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3589360339344258935">Bite sized Welsh!<br/><br/>Sometimes reading a Welsh novel can feel a bit of a slog. Not because they're poorly written (which they most certainly are not) but often because the subject matter is so dark that it's hard to maintain a sustained reading session without succumbing to darkness and despair.<br/><br/>Reheated Cabbage collects 8 unrelated short stories together and distills Welsh's dark humour into manageable bite sized pieces.<br/><br/>What I noticed most about Reheated Cabbage is that I often found myself with a g</span>
  <span id="freeText3589360339344258935" style="display:none">Bite sized Welsh!<br /><br />Sometimes reading a Welsh novel can feel a bit of a slog. Not because they're poorly written (which they most certainly are not) but often because the subject matter is so dark that it's hard to maintain a sustained reading session without succumbing to darkness and despair.<br /><br />Reheated Cabbage collects 8 unrelated short stories together and distills Welsh's dark humour into manageable bite sized pieces.<br /><br />What I noticed most about Reheated Cabbage is that I often found myself with a grin on my face. The stories contained, although typically dark, are often humorous and packed full of anti-heroes that Welsh has an amazing ability of bringing alive.<br /><br />The standout stories for me were:<br /><br />Elspeth's Boyfriend - This tells the story of a Christmas round at the Begbie homestead. If like me, you we're left disappointed by the lack of Begbie in Skagboys then this should quell your craving for his particular brand of insanity and violence as he squares up to his sisters new boyfriend. Hilarious throughout.<br /><br />The Rosewell Incident - What would happen if Aliens visited earth and abducted a single Scottish football hooligan as a representation of the human race? Well this story likes to answer that question. Needless to say, drug addicted aliens, anal probes, memory wipes and inter-species copulations all make an appearance in this amusing tale of one mans dream to elevate his firm to not just to the top of the Scottish rankings, but those of Earth.<br /><br />I Am Miami - This picks up after the events of Glue (probably my favourite Welsh novel). It was great dropping in on N-Sign and Juice Terry once again and their interactions with a one Mr Black, their old high school teacher/nemesis. A fantastic tales of forgiveness, trust, relationships, religion and love.<br /><br /><br />Overall, a highly enjoyable read that I'd recommend to any Welsh fan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3589360339344258935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14771003000091772913">The title of this book really says it all.   <span id="freeText14771003000091772913" style="display:none">The title of this book really says it all. Most of the stories are really very dull and uninteresting, and kind of confusing because it becomes tough to keep track of which character from Welsh's universe we're learning more about. <br /><br />One story, about aliens who learned everything they know about Earth from one of Welsh's hooligans had promise, but it simply didn't live up to that promise, and fell kind of flat.       <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review987887872">

<div id="review_1774494446" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1774494446" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47493995-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452141155p2/47493995.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1774494446?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/47493995-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099506997" href="/book/show/8861534-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47493995-rob?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1774494446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16807077259777552036">A hodgepodge of B-sides from a writer used to walking the knife's edge of brilliance and blunder. Here he fails spectacularly. It's all mere filler, or worse, like some crude bootleg of an artist justiably renowned for genius. Poor pacing, casual and gratuitous sex, drugs and violence; a flimsy effort. The worst offenders are yawn-inducing gutter drips that just don't land... Indeed, Welsh ruefully calls this cash grab "Reheated Cabbage". Aye, we were warned...</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R7835" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R7835" href="/user/show/31459324-r7835">R7835</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11241739-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31459324-r7835?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31459324-r7835?shelf=calibre">calibre</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3557885672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7565855671895285651">At his worst, Irvine Welsh reminds me of a Poundland version of Selby Jr, which he manages to be here quite a lot. Reheated Cabbage is the perfect name for this collection of stories.<br/><br/>A Fault on the Line - 2.5/5. This was just a joke - a negative stereotype of Scottish life turned up to 11. It was funny, but it's a throwaway. Quite a good way to get you hooked into reading the rest of the stories, though.<br/><br/>Catholic Guilt - 2.5/5. This one had a bit more legs, but again, it's a bit of a joke. <br/><br/>Elspet</span>
  <span id="freeText7565855671895285651" style="display:none">At his worst, Irvine Welsh reminds me of a Poundland version of Selby Jr, which he manages to be here quite a lot. Reheated Cabbage is the perfect name for this collection of stories.<br /><br />A Fault on the Line - 2.5/5. This was just a joke - a negative stereotype of Scottish life turned up to 11. It was funny, but it's a throwaway. Quite a good way to get you hooked into reading the rest of the stories, though.<br /><br />Catholic Guilt - 2.5/5. This one had a bit more legs, but again, it's a bit of a joke. <br /><br />Elspeth's Boyfriend - 3/5. A Christmas day with Francis is every bit as terrifying as you'd imagine. <br /><br />Kissing and Making Up - 2/5. What was the point of this? I quite like it when scenes that never made a novel are released in short stories. It's a bit like watching deleted scenes of your favourite show/film. But this didn't do anything for me.<br /><br />The Rosewell Incident - 2.5/5. This was a let down. It feels like Welsh came up with this and wrote it all in the same day and just left it as it was - the story doesn't really go anywhere, it's more of an off-the-cuff ramble. Some of it was ok/funny, but overall it fell a bit flat.<br /><br />The State of the Party - 3.5/5. I liked this one. I thought Welsh did a good job of capturing the paranoia of the characters.<br /><br />Victor Spoils - 3/5. This one was quite good, too. Like The State of the Party, I would like to have read more of this.<br /><br />I Am Miami - 4/5. This was good, and probably the strongest writing of the lot. Old School 😁<br /><br />Fans of Welsh will find something to enjoy from this collection. Newcomers beware. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7565855671895285651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1992435784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1992435784" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1885651-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433859438p2/1885651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1992435784?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/1885651-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338027" href="/book/show/6570524-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1885651-tom?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1992435784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12087267196992386413">As a huge fan of Irvine Welsh, I jumped at the opportunity to snag this collection of short stories when I saw it the local thrift store for a few bucks. I didn't expect it to rival any of his best works, but figured I can never have too many Welsh books in my library. I was right, these stories maybe aren't his best, but it's classic Welsh, through and through. There's the humorous, colloquial banter in Scots dialect (which by now I am fully versed in), there's the excess of booze and drugs and</span>
  <span id="freeText12087267196992386413" style="display:none">As a huge fan of Irvine Welsh, I jumped at the opportunity to snag this collection of short stories when I saw it the local thrift store for a few bucks. I didn't expect it to rival any of his best works, but figured I can never have too many Welsh books in my library. I was right, these stories maybe aren't his best, but it's classic Welsh, through and through. There's the humorous, colloquial banter in Scots dialect (which by now I am fully versed in), there's the excess of booze and drugs and Football references, and the plots and scenarios that waver from the extreme, so-absurd-it's-hilarious to the more grounded and gritty. And fans will notice some cameos from Trainspotting and Glue alumni, including everyone's psychopath, Francis Begbie. All in all a pretty good read with a couple standout stories, but I would really only recommend this to the passionate fans who have exhausted his best material and are looking elsewhere to satisfy their Welsh fix.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12087267196992386413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14823140709651024245" style="display:none">Bukowski anyone? I was given this by my housemate and though I really enjoyed some of the stories that came later in the book, the one about aliens was just drivel (you get the feeling Welsh thought of that one when he was fourteen and bored out of his skull and just polished it up for the current book), and I ended up feeling really sorry for the author because apparently everyone he knows is an utter self-centered asshole at heart. <div id="review_3366935540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3366935540" />
    <a title="Dario" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52381300-dario"><img alt="Dario" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586496583p2/52381300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3366935540?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dario" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dario" href="/user/show/52381300-dario">Dario</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11241739-reheated-cabbage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52381300-dario?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52381300-dario?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52381300-dario?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3366935540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14590247067173552532">I don’t have much to say about this, other than I really enjoyed these eight short stories. I forgot how great Welsh was at coming up with these slice-of-life vignettes made up of intoxicated, alcoholic, violent and life-questioning characters.<br/><br/>My two favourite stories were <i>Elspeth’s Boyfriend</i> and <i>The State of the Party</i>. The former is a Christmas story. The latter is like <i>Weekend at Bernie’s</i>, but set (of course) on a night out in Edinburgh.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3502555081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3502555081" />
    <a title="Jay Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/120080425-jay-thomas"><img alt="Jay Thomas" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay Thomas" href="/user/show/120080425-jay-thomas">Jay Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3502555081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1444066941248821514">This was my first Irvine Welsh book, and I can safely say that I will be picking him up again. I picked it up after re-watching Trainspotting (which is one of my favourite films of all time) and found it to be a highly interesting read. <br/>Every story in this collection is extremely dark, as well as pure genius. Looking for a dark comedy about ordinary working class people in extraordinary situations? This is the collection for you. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jrregMpSep3rtGvMlEJqVhgJW4nSxJCKWxpZhAlxcsf6G/EkYx5z5XD88pJLBTu42JzBjme296ghoBwxu7rp5w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('u6kZKSjjylIo9T4QJyRiS4mM2vFOV2hMuGwAxgGn4LjPCDaNga/DKrO9p074YzOlSRlA9vslD27C1kVzs2x7mA==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_373687'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373687.Baise_Moi?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Baise-Moi<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/35668.Virginie_Despentes?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Virginie Despentes<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.35 avg rating &mdash; 2,654 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1993\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer8021526478255508533\">Baise-Moi is one of the most controversial French novels of recent years, a punk fantasy that takes female rage to its outer limits. Now the basis for a hit underground film which was banned in France, Baise-Moi is a searing story of two women on a r<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8021526478255508533\" style=\"display:none\">Baise-Moi is one of the most controversial French novels of recent years, a punk fantasy that takes female rage to its outer limits. Now the basis for a hit underground film which was banned in France, Baise-Moi is a searing story of two women on a rampage that is part Thelma and Louise, part Viking conquest. Manu and Nadine have had all they can take. Manu has been brutally raped, and determines it\'s not worth leaving anything precious lying vulnerable -- including her very self. She teams up with Nadine, a nihilist who watches pornography incessantly, and they enact their own version of les vols et les viols (rape and pillage) -- they lure men sexually, use them up, then rob and kill them. Drawing from the spiky cadences of the Sex Pistols and the murderous eroticism of Georges Bataille or Dennis Cooper, Baise-Moi is a shocking, accomplished, and truly unforgettable novel.<\/span>\n  <a The Insult is about a man blinded by a robber in a supermarket parking lot who discovers one night that--because of a bizarre experiment--he can see again. Thomson\'s latest finds three very different characters--an aimless waitress, a reluctant hit man, and an ambitious young marketing executive--linked by the sudden success of a new soft drink. But a closer look confirms the feeling that Soft! continues the author\'s fascination with the way science can bend and shape the destinies of all sorts of nonscientific people. Certainly Glade Spencer, the flaky young woman who flies off periodically for unpleasant encounters with her American lawyer boyfriend, has no idea when she signs up for a sleep clinic to earn some extra cash that the soda slogans planted in her brain could cause her death. Barker Dodds, the nightclub bouncer from Plymouth, doesn\'t know why he\'s being paid to kill Glade. And James Lyle, the striving marketer who thought up the brainwashing scheme in the first place, is deliberately out of the loop about its consequences. All three are so perfectly drawn that you\'d recognize them on the street, and the way Thomson describes their quirky, weirdly decorated flats and lifestyles captures the flickering pulse of London <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12314113380875064611">Probably most famous for his gritty depiction of a gang of Scottish Heroin addicts, <i>Trainspotting</i> (1993), Welsh focuses on the darker side of human nature and drug use. All of his novels are set in his native Scotland and filled with anti-heroes, small time crooks and hooligans. Welsh manages, however to imbue these characters with a sad humanity that makes them likable despite their obvious scumb</span>
  <span id="freeText12314113380875064611" style="display:none">Probably most famous for his gritty depiction of a gang of Scottish Heroin addicts, <i>Trainspotting</i> (1993), Welsh focuses on the darker side of human nature and drug use. All of his novels are set in his native Scotland and filled with anti-heroes, small time crooks and hooligans. Welsh manages, however to imbue these characters with a sad humanity that makes them likable despite their obvious scumbaggerry. Irvine Welsh is also known for writing in his native Edinburgh Scots dialect, making his prose challenging for the average reader unfamiliar with this style.</span>
